<div id="review_138620600" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/138620600" />
    <a title="Angie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50378-angie"><img alt="Angie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510342996p2/50378.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/138620600?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angie" href="/user/show/50378-angie">Angie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781402241376" href="/book/show/8495173-the-winter-sea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=good-uns">good-uns</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer138620600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6066908815419072982">I've seen <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/486812.Susanna_Kearsley' title='Susanna Kearsley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Susanna Kearsley</a>'s name pop up hither and yon around the blogosphere for going on a year now. I added her name to my list of authors to check out awhile back and I've spent the intervening time idly wondered whether the enticing comparisons to the likes of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15590.Mary_Stewart' title='Mary Stewart' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mary Stewart</a> had some merit. Not long ago I decided THE WINTER SEA would be the perfect maiden voyage with Kearsley. Published a couple of years ago in the UK, the U.S. edition was slated to come out December 1st and I added it to my</span>
  <span id="freeText6066908815419072982" style="display:none">I've seen <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/486812.Susanna_Kearsley" title="Susanna Kearsley" rel="nofollow noopener">Susanna Kearsley</a>'s name pop up hither and yon around the blogosphere for going on a year now. I added her name to my list of authors to check out awhile back and I've spent the intervening time idly wondered whether the enticing comparisons to the likes of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15590.Mary_Stewart" title="Mary Stewart" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary Stewart</a> had some merit. Not long ago I decided THE WINTER SEA would be the perfect maiden voyage with Kearsley. Published a couple of years ago in the UK, the U.S. edition was slated to come out December 1st and I added it to my Christmas list in the hopes it might find its way inside my stocking this year. Happily, I was not disappointed and I have my mother to thank for that--another die-hard <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15590.Mary_Stewart" title="Mary Stewart" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary Stewart</a> fan herself. So I picked it up the night after Christmas and settled in to see what all the fuss was about. Well, it quickly became crystal clear to me why people love her work. THE WINTER SEA is the perfectly captivating kind of historical fiction that casts its spell over you from page one and doesn't let go until all is eloquently said and done.<br /><br />Carrie McClelland is a famous writer of historical fiction. She works best in isolation and frequently travels to the destinations featured in her novels to absorb the local flavor and engage in primary research for the events, history, and people that make up her stories. After an extended period in France, frustrated with the lack of progress she's making on her current manuscript, Carrie agrees to take a break to attend the blessing of her agent's newborn baby in Scotland. On her way up the coast, she stumbles across the ruins of a beautiful castle as she stops to ask for directions. Something about the place seems to call to her. She longs to stay but convinces herself to continue on to her friend's house. Little does she know she'll be returning to Cruden Bay very soon indeed as Castle Slains plays a pivotal role in her chosen tale set during the oft-overlooked Jacobite rebellion of 1708. On the advice of her agent, and the ethereal tugs she continues to feel herself, Carrie rents a tiny cottage on the coast and settles in to let the muse have her way with her. But the closer she delves into the history of Slains, the deeper she is drawn into the lives of its long-dead inhabitants. The characters of her story begin to take on a life of their own and Carrie is no longer sure what is fact and what is fiction as she rushes to get down all the images and conversations bombarding her on a daily basis.<br /><br />What a beautiful and engrossing story! I'm awfully fond of historical fiction set during any of the Jacobite rebellions. Ever since reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8659.Jennifer_Roberson" title="Jennifer Roberson" rel="nofollow noopener">Jennifer Roberson</a>'s excellent <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/481645.Lady_Of_The_Glen_A_Novel_of_17Th_Century_Scotland_and_the_Massacre_of_Glencoe" title="Lady Of The Glen A Novel of 17Th-Century Scotland and the Massacre of Glencoe by Jennifer Roberson" rel="nofollow noopener">Lady of the Glen</a> several years ago, I've found the time period and subject matter fascinating, if incredibly bittersweet. This story is no exception. The narrative alternates between the present day and the events leading up to and following the failed rebellion in 1708. Though the story and characters in the past start out as Carrie's own creation, she uses one of her own ancestors as her heroine, and in doing so unwittingly forges a bridge of shared memory between them. The results are unexpected and truly riveting. I never knew for sure which way the chips would fall and whether or not the novel as a whole would cross over into a supernatural/time travel extravaganza a la <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10964.Outlander__Outlander___1_" title="Outlander (Outlander, #1) by Diana Gabaldon" rel="nofollow noopener">Outlander</a> or if there would be a less outlandish explanation for the unfathomable link between these two women. I won't spill the beans here, but will say that I was very pleased (and relieved) at the outcome and heartily approve of the deft manner in which Ms. Kearsley handled both the slightly fantastical element to her story as well as the two primary relationships flourishing therein. I initially thought I would get bored with the ancestor Sophia's story, as I was immediately so caught up in Carrie's present-day tale. But that worry quickly fled as I eagerly looked forward to each switch of narration to find out how my other people were faring. Carrie's growing relationship with a very endearing local history lecturer had me at hello and Sophia's perilous and earnest attachment to a young Scottish soldier had me on the edge of my seat. In retrospect, I do wish we'd gotten a more extended resolution for Carrie and her suitor, but overall I closed the book extremely satisfied with the way the relationships concluded. THE WINTER SEA will appeal in spades to fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15590.Mary_Stewart" title="Mary Stewart" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary Stewart</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3617.Diana_Gabaldon" title="Diana Gabaldon" rel="nofollow noopener">Diana Gabaldon</a>. And, not to annoy any <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10964.Outlander__Outlander___1_" title="Outlander (Outlander, #1) by Diana Gabaldon" rel="nofollow noopener">Outlander</a> fans out there but I, for one, infinitely prefer Kearsley's reserved and resonant touch to the the rampant floridity of Gabaldon's epic. Highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6066908815419072982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_241573965" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241573965" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1394928-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405367803p2/1394928.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/241573965?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/1394928-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=friend-love">friend-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=hf">hf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=audible">audible</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=friend-rec">friend-rec</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=bricks">bricks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=ashley-s-list">ashley-s-list</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer241573965" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4358062689165455943">4.5 stars. This is a classic case of the right book finding the right time. I know I've picked this book up several times with the intent to read it and it just didn't look all that compelling. Nothing really grabbed me about it beyond the cover, I didn't really know much about that historical period, and I'm not really a person who reads romance novels regularly. I'd read a kind of heavy, dark book though and needed something light. A friend recommended something short that was perfect. I enjoy</span>
  <span id="freeText4358062689165455943" style="display:none">4.5 stars. This is a classic case of the right book finding the right time. I know I've picked this book up several times with the intent to read it and it just didn't look all that compelling. Nothing really grabbed me about it beyond the cover, I didn't really know much about that historical period, and I'm not really a person who reads romance novels regularly. I'd read a kind of heavy, dark book though and needed something light. A friend recommended something short that was perfect. I enjoyed it, but wanted something still on the light side but longer. She suggested this one and this book finally found its time. <br /><br />This book has two parallel storylines. One is in the present, and the other is in the early 18th century, both in Scotland, by the sea. <br /><br />Reasons to read this book:<br /><br />-This is an escape read, you'll be immersed quickly. <br />-You won't wanna put the book down. <br />-Both storylines are equally appealing, and you'll really care about the characters. <br />-It's all about relationships. Relationships of all kinds. <br />-If you're into genealogy, you'll love this book. <br />-Both male leads are hard to resist. :)<br />-If you've always wanted to write a book, this is great, because she really gets you into the mind of an author as she's creating a story that takes off in her mind. <br />-The audio narration by Rosalyn Landor was very well done. She got the Scottish accents almost too perfect, they were a bit hard to understand at times, but mainly this was one character with a minor role who had a very deep accent. The others were easy to understand. She did a great job of changing from female to male voices! At times, it was hard to believe a woman read the whole book. <br /><br />I know this is a book I will never forget. If you can get through this book without crying, you may not be totally human! I really enjoyed it, and thanks to everyone who encouraged me to read this. Perfect book, exactly what I needed. Proof that we should be able to go to the library or bookstore and get a prescription in literary form. This was it for me! <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4358062689165455943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5512657-sara?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5512657-sara?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5512657-sara?shelf=pleasure-reading">pleasure-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5512657-sara?shelf=2018-aty-challenge">2018-aty-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5512657-sara?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5512657-sara?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5512657-sara?shelf=borrowed-from-library">borrowed-from-library</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2410281704" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer67425953933008005">4.5 I haven't enjoyed a book this much in a long time stars.<br/><br/>Reading Susanna Kearsley is such fun. I find that I both want to read faster so that I can see what will happen and read slower so that I can stay in this story and this world just a little bit longer. She sifts in just the right amount of romance, mystery and history to make a perfect cake, and she is one of the few writers who can keep me as interested in the modern-day story she is telling as the historical one. I typically find myse</span>
  <span id="freeText67425953933008005" style="display:none">4.5 I haven't enjoyed a book this much in a long time stars.<br /><br />Reading Susanna Kearsley is such fun. I find that I both want to read faster so that I can see what will happen and read slower so that I can stay in this story and this world just a little bit longer. She sifts in just the right amount of romance, mystery and history to make a perfect cake, and she is one of the few writers who can keep me as interested in the modern-day story she is telling as the historical one. I typically find myself just wanting to get back to the past, but with Kearsley I am happy to follow the present as well.<br /><br />This story begins with Carrie McClelland, who is writing a historical novel set in 1708 and dealing with the failed attempt to put James Stewart back on the throne in Scotland. The novel is meant to be about Nathaniel Hooke, an Irishman who is in the thick of the action at the time, but when Carrie decides to include a character named after her own ancestor, Sophia Paterson, she seems to lose control of the story to the events of the past. <br /><br />The dynamics of writing a historical novel is something Kearsley obviously knows everything about, the research she does is meticulous and adds complete credence to her tale, and her handling of characters and dialogue is both charming and believable. I had determined to read all of her books after finding my first encounter with her so enjoyable--this book has convinced me that I made a great decision.<br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_272781378" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/272781378" />
    <a title="Dem" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2752994-dem"><img alt="Dem" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552868566p2/2752994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/272781378?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dem" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dem" href="/user/show/2752994-dem">Dem</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer272781378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10200550202696811194">The Winter Sea by Susanna Kearsley really seemed like a book I would love as it dealt with a part of Scottish history that I was not familiar with. I had not read a book set in Scotland before and was eager to get started on this novel after reading the fascinating blurb. <br/><br/> "In the spring of 1708 an invading Jacobite fleet of French and Scottish soldiers nearly succeeded in landing the exiled James Stewart in Scotland to reclaim his crown. Now Carrie Mc Clelland hopes to turn the stroy into her n</span>
  <span id="freeText10200550202696811194" style="display:none">The Winter Sea by Susanna Kearsley really seemed like a book I would love as it dealt with a part of Scottish history that I was not familiar with. I had not read a book set in Scotland before and was eager to get started on this novel after reading the fascinating blurb. <br /><br /> "In the spring of 1708 an invading Jacobite fleet of French and Scottish soldiers nearly succeeded in landing the exiled James Stewart in Scotland to reclaim his crown. Now Carrie Mc Clelland hopes to turn the stroy into her next bestselling novel. Settling herself in the shawow of Slains Castle she creates a heroine named for one of her own ancestors and starts to write. But when she discovers her novel is more fact than fiction, Carrie wonders if she might be dealing with ancestral memory making her the only living person who knows the truth. The ultimate betrayal that happened all those years ago and that knowledge comes very close to destroying her"<br /><br />The setting and mood of this novel is wonderful and I would have to congratulate the author on creating such wonderful settlings and giving the reader such vivid descriptions of characters and scenery, I for one was in the settling of all these scenes and had clear images of Slains Castle in my head and really enjoyed this aspect of the novel so much.<br />This is a really well researched novel about the Jacobite Rebellion. I found myself having to reread paragraphs to get people and happenings straight in my head as sometimes I found it a little difficult to follow. <br /><br />While I really enjoyed the historical side of this novel and enjoyed reading about the Jacobite invasion I did find the social history of the time very lacking and I would loved to have learned more about spirit, manners, and social conditions of 1708 but felt that was very much left out of this novel and I found this disappointing.<br /><br />The ending of the book for me was terrible. I really found it too much and not at all be believable or in keeping with the story that went before and it actually left me feeling a little cheated.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10200550202696811194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1420342393692357990"><b>***** 5 Stars *****</b><br/> <br/><b>
  <i>"For if there was no winter, we could never hope for spring."</i>
</b><br/><br/>I'm speechless. I didn't think I'd end up enjoying this book, but I became obsessed with the romance and history. <br/><br/>Carrie is a talented author working on her next novel. As she's traveling around, she feels an odd pull towards the ruins of Slains Castle. A pull so strong, she stops everything to focus on its past. <br/><br/>Throughout her research, she receives unexplainable memories and dreams about the past.... Sophie's </span>
  <span id="freeText1420342393692357990" style="display:none"><b>***** 5 Stars *****</b><br> <br><b>
  <i>"For if there was no winter, we could never hope for spring."</i>
</b><br><br>I'm speechless. I didn't think I'd end up enjoying this book, but I became obsessed with the romance and history. <br><br>Carrie is a talented author working on her next novel. As she's traveling around, she feels an odd pull towards the ruins of Slains Castle. A pull so strong, she stops everything to focus on its past. <br><br>Throughout her research, she receives unexplainable memories and dreams about the past.... Sophie's past. Reality gets blurred and deep secrets are revealed. <br><br>This book involves two stories. Two stories that I found to be equally addicting. I couldn't put this down. I've shed actual tears reading this. It's full of romance and heartbreak. Susanna Kearsley proves that you can have a wonderful romantic story without containing dirty sex scenes. I can't wait to read her other books!<br><br><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/CLOUD9BOOKSBLOG/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478105605i/21032403.png" width="60" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="http://cloud9books.blogspot.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478105673i/21032412.png" width="60" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/CLOUD9BOOKS/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478105875i/21032445.png" width="60" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_29550514" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/29550514" />
    <a title="LJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/250195-lj"><img alt="LJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436467895p2/250195.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/29550514?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LJ" href="/user/show/250195-lj">LJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=female_author">female_author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=1700s">1700s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=contemporary_post_1945">contemporary_post_1945</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=scotland">scotland</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=jacobian_1603-1714">jacobian_1603-1714</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=multiple_periods">multiple_periods</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer29550514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16076931651112177267">THE WINTER SEA (Dual-period novel/Romance-Carrie McClelland-Scotland-Cont/1708) - Ex <br/>Kearsley, Susanna – Standalone <br/>Allison & Busby, Ltd., 2008, UK Hardcover – ISBN: 9780749080976 <br/><br/>First Sentence: It wasn’t chance.<br/><br/>Bestselling author Carrie McClelland comes from France, where she is working on a book related to the 1708 attempted return of James Stewart to regain his throne. On the way to the christening of her friend and agent’s baby, she takes a side road and is drawn to Slains Castle. <br/><br/>Deciding </span>
  <span id="freeText16076931651112177267" style="display:none">THE WINTER SEA (Dual-period novel/Romance-Carrie McClelland-Scotland-Cont/1708) - Ex <br />Kearsley, Susanna – Standalone <br />Allison &amp; Busby, Ltd., 2008, UK Hardcover – ISBN: 9780749080976 <br /><br />First Sentence: It wasn’t chance.<br /><br />Bestselling author Carrie McClelland comes from France, where she is working on a book related to the 1708 attempted return of James Stewart to regain his throne. On the way to the christening of her friend and agent’s baby, she takes a side road and is drawn to Slains Castle. <br /><br />Deciding to move from France to Scotland, she rents a cottage new Slain and finds her connection to the old castle is closer even than her ancestor who once lived there.<br /><br />This is not a gothic, time travel or a torrid romance. It is a flawlessly crafted novel set in two time periods with a romantic relationship in each. From the first page, I was immersed in the story. Kearsley’s sense of place is evocative; I was with the characters in sight, sound and even smell. <br /><br />Her characters became real to me. In the present day, Carrie is a wonderful protagonist; smart and independent, as is Sophie in the past. Surrounded by a strong group of supporting characters, I felt I could sit down and have a chat with any of them. The plot is so well done and flows beautifully between the two time periods. <br /><br />Kearsley is an excellent writer. There is a lot of factual information in the story, but it is incorporated as part of the story and through dialogue; thus never taking you out of the story or causing you to question her facts. After the end of the story, she very clear about what liberties she did take, and those were few. The explanation used for the link from the present to the past was fascinating and one with which I was unfamiliar. <br /><br />At the same time, there was nothing dry about this book; I did laugh, I did cry, at times, my heart beat a bit faster from suspense and romance and I absolutely loved the endings. Not normally one to do comparisons but I believe fans of Diana Gabaldon, and Mary Stewart, and others, would enjoy this book; not to mention Ms. Kearsley’s existing fans. I wish her books were more frequent but, for another of Ms. Kearsley’s books, I’m willing to wait. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16076931651112177267" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5705329178792190737">This is the story about an author named Carrie, who writes historical fiction novels. She travels to Scotland to research Slains Castle for her newest novel and to spend some time with her editor who lives there. While she is there the characters of her book come alive in her memory. "The Winter Sea" jumps back and forth </span>
  <span id="freeText5705329178792190737" style="display:none">This is the story about an author named Carrie, who writes historical fiction novels. She travels to Scotland to research Slains Castle for her newest novel and to spend some time with her editor who lives there. While she is there the characters of her book come alive in her memory. She is actually remembering the life of her ancestor, Sophie Paterson and her marriage to John Murray. While writing her book she meets a man named Graham and a romance starts. "The Winter Sea" jumps back and forth from the story Carrie is writing to Carrie's life in the present as she writes the story. I enjoyed reading about Carrie's romance, but reading the parts that were Carrie's book bored me. In the end it turns out that Graham is actually a descendant of Sophie Patterson as well. Carrie and Graham are kissing cousins! Cool....     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_278502805" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/278502805" />
    <a title="Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4542979-kim"><img alt="Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454402751p2/4542979.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/278502805?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/4542979-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" " href="/book/show/10074752-the-winter-sea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4542979-kim?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4542979-kim?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer278502805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1455081782938361287"><br/>This is yet another book which I probably would not have read had it not been for reviews on Goodreads and recommendations from several GR friends which prompted me to read another novel by Kearsley, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/65086.Every_Secret_Thing__Kate_Murray___1_' title='Every Secret Thing (Kate Murray, #1) by Emma Cole' rel='nofollow noopener'>Every Secret Thing</a>. I liked <i> Every Secret Thing</i> enough to want to read more of Kearsley’s work. <br/><br/>This novel has dual time lines. There is a contemporary narrative, told in the first person. The narrator is an author writing a historical novel about a failed Jacobite rebellion which took place in 1708</span>
  <span id="freeText1455081782938361287" style="display:none"><br />This is yet another book which I probably would not have read had it not been for reviews on Goodreads and recommendations from several GR friends which prompted me to read another novel by Kearsley, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/65086.Every_Secret_Thing__Kate_Murray___1_" title="Every Secret Thing (Kate Murray, #1) by Emma Cole" rel="nofollow noopener">Every Secret Thing</a>. I liked <i> Every Secret Thing</i> enough to want to read more of Kearsley’s work. <br /><br />This novel has dual time lines. There is a contemporary narrative, told in the first person. The narrator is an author writing a historical novel about a failed Jacobite rebellion which took place in 1708. There is also a third person narrative set in 1708, which is the novel being written by the first person narrator. <br /><br />The novel has some very attractive features: a beautiful and romantic Scottish setting, evidence of excellent research into the rebellion, clear prose and solid development of character. However, there are some features of the novel which I found less successful, in particular, the concept of genetic memory, which is the device used to link the present-day first person narrative with the third person historical narrative. While some way to link the two narratives was obviously needed, in my view the idea that the present day author was channeling the memories of her ancestor was not convincing. <br /><br />This is a novel I probably would have liked much more had I been familiar with the history with which it deals, or the location in which it is set. That said, it has certainly made me interested in learning more about the history. It has also put Slains Castle and Cruden Bay firmly on the list of places I’d like to visit in the future. For me, this was slightly less engaging than <i>Every Secret Thing</i>, which makes it a solid 3-1/2 star read. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1455081782938361287" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2313793547" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2313793547" />
    <a title="Blackjack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3723743-blackjack"><img alt="Blackjack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1497910558p2/3723743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2313793547?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Blackjack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Blackjack" href="/user/show/3723743-blackjack">Blackjack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35894505-the-winter-sea">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2313793547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7923657023863173982">My first Kearsley novel and it was such a captivating reading experience. She is an elegant writer, and though the story has some slower scenes where not a great deal happens in terms of plot, I still felt very engaged and drawn into the worlds she is creating. I really liked too the dual stories and perspectives. <br/><br/>The contemporary setting features Canadian historical novelist, Carrie McClellan, who has been attempting to jumpstart a new book project without much luck - that is until she arrives </span>
  <span id="freeText7923657023863173982" style="display:none">My first Kearsley novel and it was such a captivating reading experience. She is an elegant writer, and though the story has some slower scenes where not a great deal happens in terms of plot, I still felt very engaged and drawn into the worlds she is creating. I really liked too the dual stories and perspectives. <br /><br />The contemporary setting features Canadian historical novelist, Carrie McClellan, who has been attempting to jumpstart a new book project without much luck - that is until she arrives in Scotland to visit her publicist and sets eyes on Slains Castle on the rugged coast of a small village. For unknown reasons, the castle compels her to stay for a while and figure out why she can envision so clearly events that took place there more than 300 years earlier. I found the concept of genetic memory quite believable in this story for it turns out that Carrie's ancestors lived at Slains and she shares their memories of an historic Jacobite uprising for which history books have paid scant attention. Villagers, family, and friends are all perplexed at how Carrie is able to unearth small details about the Scots uprisings and attempts to unseat the English monarch, and Carrie is loath to share her belief that she is able to live the events vicariously for fear of being mocked. Carrie is unexpectedly successful in resurrecting the past and is able to produce a thrilling novel out of her experiences here. Additionally, she has a lovely romance with a Scottish history lecturer, and their romance is very adult and angst-free and just utterly pleasurable to witness.<br /><br />There is a strong romance set in the past too that is the complete opposite of the drama-free romance Carrie enjoys. The romance between Sophia and John Moray is a downright nail biter at times as they really are the epitome of war-torn lovers. I found that the contrast between these two romance stories worked well together to create just the right amount of tension. There is one quite sad event that happens but is left rather open-ended, for which I take it that <i>The Firebird</i> picks up right after the events of this book. Not sure why I have put off reading Kearsley for so long but I'm happy to have a new author to read.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7923657023863173982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;

    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('y2LPYHGJbyxX48sYWXaqScXcePPkI8/LMu4T8F/ZrVlKG+SXFYeNlLbAn/bnVsCN62uxP7Mq98Xv4VGiembOtQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('d0u9wpjM19IiVfmH0XAUQ5/OsUH9v/pAQeP7NQEAb7D2MpY1/MI1asN2rWlvUH6HsXl4jaq2wk6c7LlnJL8MXA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17646657873145482698">New York Times, USA Today, and Globe and Mail bestselling author Susanna Kearsley is a former museum curator who loves restoring the lost voices of real people to the page, interweaving romance and historical intrigue with modern adventure. <br/><br/>Her books, published in translation in more than 20 countries, have won the Catherine Cookson Fiction Prize, RT Reviewers’ Choice Awards, a RITA Award, and Nat</span>
  <span id="freeText17646657873145482698" style="display:none">New York Times, USA Today, and Globe and Mail bestselling author Susanna Kearsley is a former museum curator who loves restoring the lost voices of real people to the page, interweaving romance and historical intrigue with modern adventure. <br /><br />Her books, published in translation in more than 20 countries, have won the Catherine Cookson Fiction Prize, RT Reviewers’ Choice Awards, a RITA Award, and National Readers’ Choice Awards, and have finaled for the UK’s Romantic Novel of the Year and the Crime Writers of Canada's Arthur Ellis Award for Best Novel.<br /><br />She lives near Toronto, Ontario, Canada.<br /><br />(Aka <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3270732.Emma_Cole" title="Emma Cole" rel="nofollow noopener">Emma Cole</a>, a pseudonym she used for one novel, Every Secret Thing, a thriller which at the time was intended to be the first of a trilogy featuring heroine Kate Murray, and which may yet be finished, some day. Meantime, Every Secret Thing has been reissued under Kearsley's name, and the Emma Cole pseudonym is no longer in use.) </span>
  <a data-text-id="17646657873145482698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

    go = function () {
      for (i = 0; i < n; i += 1) {
        script = d.createElement('SCRIPT');
        script.type = 'text/javascript';
        script.async = true;
        script.src = load[i];
        first.parentNode.insertBefore(script, first);
      }
    }
  if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,

     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

</script>
